href="/wiki/Bacteria" title="Bacteria">Bacteria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Archaea" title="Archaea">Archaea</a>, and  <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eukaryota" title="Eukaryota">Eukaryota</a>. All are microorganisms except some eukaryote groups.</div></div></div>
<p>Single-celled microorganisms were the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Origin_of_life" title="Origin of life">first forms of life</a> to develop on Earth, approximately 3–4 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gigaannum" title="Gigaannum">billion years</a> ago.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[32]</a></sup> Further evolution was slow,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[33]</a></sup> and for about 3 billion years in the <a href="/wiki/Precambrian" title="Precambrian">Precambrian</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eon_(geology)" title="Eon (geology)">eon</a>, (much of the history of <a href="/wiki/Life" title="Life">life on Earth</a>), all <a href="/wiki/Organism" title="Organism">organisms</a> were microorganisms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[35]</a></sup> Bacteria, algae and fungi have been identified in <a href="/wiki/Amber" title="Amber">amber</a> that is 220 million years old, which shows that the <a href="/wiki/Morphology_(biology)" title="Morphology (biology)">morphology</a> of microorganisms has changed little since the <a href="/wiki/Triassic" title="Triassic">Triassic</a> period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[36]</a></sup> The newly discovered <a href="/wiki/Nickel#Biological_role" title="Nickel">biological role played by nickel</a>, however — especially that brought about by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Types_of_volcanic_eruption" title="Types of volcanic eruption">volcanic eruptions</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Siberian_Traps" title="Siberian Traps">Siberian Traps</a> — may have accelerated the evolution of <a href="/wiki/Methanogen" title="Methanogen">methanogens</a> towards the end of the <a href="/wiki/Permian%E2%80%93Triassic_extinction_event" title="Permian–Triassic extinction event">Permian–Triassic extinction event</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[37]</a></sup>
</p><p>Microorganisms tend to have a relatively fast rate of evolution. Most microorganisms can reproduce rapidly, and bacteria are also able to freely exchange genes through <a href="/wiki/Bacterial_conjugation" title="Bacterial conjugation">conjugation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Transformation_(genetics)" title="Transformation (genetics)">transformation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Transduction_(genetics)" title="Transduction (genetics)">transduction</a>, even between widely divergent species.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[38]</a></sup> This <a href="/wiki/Horizontal_gene_transfer" title="Horizontal gene transfer">horizontal gene transfer</a>, coupled with a high <a href="/wiki/Mutation" title="Mutation">mutation</a> rate and other means of transformation, allows microorganisms to swiftly <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biological_evolution" title="Biological evolution">evolve</a> (via <a href="/wiki/Natural_selection" title="Natural selection">natural selection</a>) to survive in new environments and respond to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stressors" title="Stressors">environmental stresses</a>. This rapid evolution is important in medicine, as it has led to the development of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multidrug_resistance" title="Multidrug resistance">multidrug resistant</a> <a href="/wiki/Pathogenic_bacteria" title="Pathogenic bacteria">pathogenic bacteria</a>, <i>superbugs</i>, that are <a href="/wiki/Antimicrobial_resistance" title="Antimicrobial resistance">resistant to antibiotics</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[39]</a></sup>
</p><p>A possible transitional form of microorganism between a prokaryote and a eukaryote was discovered in 2012 by Japanese scientists. <i><a href="/wiki/Parakaryon_myojinensis" title="Parakaryon myojinensis">Parakaryon myojinensis</a></i> is a unique microorganism larger than a typical prokaryote, but with nuclear material enclosed in a membrane as in a eukaryote, and the presence of endosymbionts. This is seen to be the first plausible evolutionary form of microorganism, showing a stage of development from the prokaryote to the eukaryote.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Parakaryon_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-Parakaryon-41">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yamaguchi_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-Yamaguchi-42">[41]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Archaea">Archaea</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microorganism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Archaea">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Archaea" title="Archaea">Archaea</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Prokaryote" title="Prokaryote">Prokaryote</a></div>
<p>Archaea are <a href="/wiki/Prokaryote" title="Prokaryote">prokaryotic</a> unicellular organisms, and form the first domain of life, in <a href="/wiki/Carl_Woese" title="Carl Woese">Carl Woese</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Three-domain_system" title="Three-domain system">three-domain system</a>. A prokaryote is defined as having no <a href="/wiki/Cell_nucleus" title="Cell nucleus">cell nucleus</a> or other <a href="/wiki/Lipid_bilayer" title="Lipid bilayer">membrane bound</a>-<a href="/wiki/Organelle" title="Organelle">organelle</a>. Archaea share this defining feature with the bacteria with which they were once grouped. In 1990 the microbiologist Woese proposed the three-domain system that divided living things into bacteria, archaea and eukaryotes,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[42]</a></sup> and thereby split the prokaryote domain.
</p><p>Archaea differ from bacteria in both their genetics and biochemistry. For example, while bacterial <a href="/wiki/Cell_membrane" title="Cell membrane">cell membranes</a> are made from <a href="/wiki/Phospholipid" title="Phospholipid">phosphoglycerides</a> with <a href="/wiki/Ester" title="Ester">ester</a> bonds, archaean membranes are made of <a href="/wiki/Ether_lipid" title="Ether lipid">ether lipids</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[43]</a></sup> Archaea were originally described as <a href="/wiki/Extremophile" title="Extremophile">extremophiles</a> living in <a href="/wiki/Extreme_environment" title="Extreme environment">extreme environments</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Hot_spring" title="Hot spring">hot springs</a>, but have since been found in all types of <a href="/wiki/Habitat" title="Habitat">habitats</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[44]</a></sup> Only now are scientists beginning to realize how common archaea are in the environment, with <a href="/wiki/Crenarchaeota" title="Crenarchaeota">Crenarchaeota</a> being the most common form of life in the ocean, dominating ecosystems below 150 m in depth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[46]</a></sup> These organisms are also common in soil and play a vital role in <a href="/wiki/Ammonia" title="Ammonia">ammonia</a> oxidation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LeiningerUrich2006_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-LeiningerUrich2006-48">[47]</a></sup>
</p><p>The combined domains of archaea and bacteria make up the most diverse and abundant group of <a href="/wiki/Organism" title="Organism">organisms</a> on Earth and inhabit practically all environments where the temperature is below +140 °C. They are found in <a href="/wiki/Water" title="Water">water</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soil" title="Soil">soil</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Earth%27s_atmosphere" title="Earth's atmosphere">air</a>, as the <a href="/wiki/Microbiota" title="Microbiota">microbiome</a> of an organism, <a href="/wiki/Hot_spring" title="Hot spring">hot springs</a> and even deep beneath the Earth's crust in <a href="/wiki/Rock_(geology)" title="Rock (geology)">rocks</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gold_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gold-49">[48]</a></sup> The number of prokaryotes is estimated to be around five million trillion trillion, or 5 × 10<sup>30</sup>, accounting for at least half the <a href="/wiki/Biomass_(ecology)" title="Biomass (ecology)">biomass</a> on Earth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[49]</a></sup>
</p><p>The biodiversity of the prokaryotes is unknown, but may be very large. A May 2016 estimate, based on laws of scaling from known numbers of species against the size of organism, gives an estimate of perhaps 1 trillion species on the planet, of which most would be microorganisms. Currently, only one-thousandth of one percent of that total have been described.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NSF-2016002_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-NSF-2016002-51">[50]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bacteria">Bacteria</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microorganism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Bacteria">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bacteria" title="Bacteria">Bacteria</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Staphylococcus_aureus_01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1630" data-file-width="2100" height="171" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Staphylococcus_aureus_01.jpg/220px-Staphylococcus_aureus_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Staphylococcus_aureus_01.jpg/330px-Staphylococcus_aureus_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Staphylococcus_aureus_01.jpg/440px-Staphylococcus_aureus_01.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Staphylococcus_aureus_01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/Staphylococcus_aureus" title="Staphylococcus aureus">Staphylococcus aureus</a></i> bacteria magnified about 10,000x</div></div></div>
<p>Bacteria like archaea are prokaryotic – unicellular, and having no cell nucleus or other membrane-bound organelle. Bacteria are microscopic, with a few extremely rare exceptions, such as <i><a href="/wiki/Thiomargarita_namibiensis" title="Thiomargarita namibiensis">Thiomargarita namibiensis</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[51]</a></sup> Bacteria function and reproduce as individual cells, but they can often aggregate in multicellular <a href="/wiki/Colony_(biology)#Microbial_colony" title="Colony (biology)">colonies</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[52]</a></sup> Some species such as <a href="/wiki/Myxobacteria" title="Myxobacteria">myxobacteria</a> can aggregate into complex <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Swarm" title="Swarm">swarming</a> structures, operating as multicellular groups as part of their <a href="/wiki/Biological_life_cycle" title="Biological life cycle">life cycle</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[53]</a></sup> or form clusters in <a href="/wiki/Colony_(biology)" title="Colony (biology)">bacterial colonies</a> such as <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/E.coli" title="E.coli">E.coli</a></i>.
</p><p>Their <a href="/wiki/Genome" title="Genome">genome</a> is usually a <a href="/wiki/Circular_bacterial_chromosome" title="Circular bacterial chromosome">circular bacterial chromosome</a> – a single loop of <a href="/wiki/DNA" title="DNA">DNA</a>, although they can also harbor small pieces of DNA called <a href="/wiki/Plasmid" title="Plasmid">plasmids</a>. These plasmids can be transferred between cells through <a href="/wiki/Bacterial_conjugation" title="Bacterial conjugation">bacterial conjugation</a>. Bacteria have an enclosing <a href="/wiki/Bacterial_cell_structure#Cell_wall" title="Bacterial cell structure">cell wall</a>, which provides strength and rigidity to their cells. They reproduce by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Binary_fission" title="Binary fission">binary fission</a> or sometimes by <a href="/wiki/Budding" title="Budding">budding</a>, but do not undergo <a href="/wiki/Meiosis" title="Meiosis">meiotic</a> <a href="/wiki/Sexual_reproduction" title="Sexual reproduction">sexual reproduction</a>. However, many bacterial species can transfer DNA between individual cells by a <a href="/wiki/Horizontal_gene_transfer" title="Horizontal gene transfer">horizontal gene transfer</a> process referred to as natural <a href="/wiki/Transformation_(genetics)" title="Transformation (genetics)">transformation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[54]</a></sup> Some species form extraordinarily resilient <a href="/wiki/Endospore" title="Endospore">spores</a>, but for bacteria this is a mechanism for survival, not reproduction. Under optimal conditions bacteria can grow extremely rapidly and their numbers can double as quickly as every 20 minutes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[55]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Eukaryotes">Eukaryotes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microorganism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Eukaryotes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Eukaryote" title="Eukaryote">Eukaryote</a></div>
<p>Most living things that are visible to the naked eye in their adult form are <a href="/wiki/Eukaryote" title="Eukaryote">eukaryotes</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Human" title="Human">humans</a>. However, a large number of eukaryotes are also microorganisms. Unlike <a href="/wiki/Bacteria" title="Bacteria">bacteria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Archaea" title="Archaea">archaea</a>, eukaryotes contain <a href="/wiki/Organelle" title="Organelle">organelles</a> such as the <a href="/wiki/Cell_nucleus" title="Cell nucleus">cell nucleus</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Golgi_apparatus" title="Golgi apparatus">Golgi apparatus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mitochondrion" title="Mitochondrion">mitochondria</a> in their <a href="/wiki/Cell_(biology)" title="Cell (biology)">cells</a>. The nucleus is an organelle that houses the <a href="/wiki/DNA" title="DNA">DNA</a> that makes up a cell's genome. DNA (Deoxyribonucleic acid) itself is arranged in complex <a href="/wiki/Chromosome" title="Chromosome">chromosomes</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[56]</a></sup>
Mitochondria are organelles vital in <a href="/wiki/Metabolism" title="Metabolism">metabolism</a> as they are the site of the <a href="/wiki/Citric_acid_cycle" title="Citric acid cycle">citric acid cycle</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oxidative_phosphorylation" title="Oxidative phosphorylation">oxidative phosphorylation</a>. They evolved from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Symbiotic" title="Symbiotic">symbiotic</a> bacteria and retain a remnant genome.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dyall_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dyall-58">[57]</a></sup> Like bacteria, <a href="/wiki/Plant_cell" title="Plant cell">plant cells</a> have <a href="/wiki/Cell_wall" title="Cell wall">cell walls</a>, and contain organelles such as <a href="/wiki/Chloroplast" title="Chloroplast">chloroplasts</a> in addition to the organelles in other eukaryotes. Chloroplasts produce energy from <a href="/wiki/Light" title="Light">light</a> by <a href="/wiki/Photosynthesis" title="Photosynthesis">photosynthesis</a>, and were also originally symbiotic <a href="/wiki/Bacteria" title="Bacteria">bacteria</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dyall_58-1"><a href="#cite_note-Dyall-58">[57]</a></sup>
</p><p>Unicellular eukaryotes consist of a single <a href="/wiki/Cell_(biology)" title="Cell (biology)">cell</a> throughout their life cycle. This qualification is significant since most <a href="/wiki/Multicellular_organism" title="Multicellular organism">multicellular</a> eukaryotes consist of a single cell called a <a href="/wiki/Zygote" title="Zygote">zygote</a> only at the beginning of their life cycles. Microbial eukaryotes can be either <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Haploid" title="Haploid">haploid</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diploid" title="Diploid">diploid</a>, and some organisms have multiple <a href="/wiki/Cell_nucleus" title="Cell nucleus">cell nuclei</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[58]</a></sup>
</p><p>Unicellular eukaryotes usually reproduce asexually by <a href="/wiki/Mitosis" title="Mitosis">mitosis</a> under favorable conditions. However, under stressful conditions such as nutrient limitations and other conditions associated with DNA damage, they tend to reproduce sexually by <a href="/wiki/Meiosis" title="Meiosis">meiosis</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fertilization" title="Fertilization">syngamy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bernstein_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bernstein-60">[59]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Protists">Protists</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microorganism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Protists">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protista" title="Protista">Protista</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Euglena_mutabilis_-_400x_-_1_(10388739803)_(cropped).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="669" data-file-width="667" height="221" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Euglena_mutabilis_-_400x_-_1_%2810388739803%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Euglena_mutabilis_-_400x_-_1_%2810388739803%29_%28cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Euglena_mutabilis_-_400x_-_1_%2810388739803%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Euglena_mutabilis_-_400x_-_1_%2810388739803%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Euglena_mutabilis_-_400x_-_1_%2810388739803%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Euglena_mutabilis_-_400x_-_1_%2810388739803%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Euglena_mutabilis_-_400x_-_1_(10388739803)_(cropped).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/Euglena" title="Euglena">Euglena mutabilis</a></i>, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Photosynthetic" title="Photosynthetic">photosynthetic</a> <a href="/wiki/Flagellate" title="Flagellate">flagellate</a></div></div></div>
<p>Of <a href="/wiki/Eukaryote" title="Eukaryote">eukaryotic</a> groups, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protists" title="Protists">protists</a> are most commonly <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unicellular" title="Unicellular">unicellular</a> and microscopic. This is a highly diverse group of organisms that are not easy to classify.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[61]</a></sup> Several <a href="/wiki/Algae" title="Algae">algae</a> <a href="/wiki/Species" title="Species">species</a> are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multicellular" title="Multicellular">multicellular</a> protists, and <a href="/wiki/Slime_mold" title="Slime mold">slime molds</a> have unique life cycles that involve switching between unicellular, colonial, and multicellular forms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[62]</a></sup> The number of species of protists is unknown since only a small proportion has been identified. Protist diversity is high in oceans, deep sea-vents, river sediment and an acidic river, suggesting that many eukaryotic microbial communities may yet be discovered.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[63]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[64]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Fungi">Fungi</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microorganism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Fungi">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Fungus" title="Fungus">Fungus</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Fungus" title="Fungus">fungi</a> have several unicellular species, such as baker's yeast (<i><a href="/wiki/Saccharomyces_cerevisiae" title="Saccharomyces cerevisiae">Saccharomyces cerevisiae</a></i>) and fission yeast (<i><a href="/wiki/Schizosaccharomyces_pombe" title="Schizosaccharomyces pombe">Schizosaccharomyces pombe</a></i>). Some fungi, such as the pathogenic yeast <i><a href="/wiki/Candida_albicans" title="Candida albicans">Candida albicans</a></i>, can undergo <a href="/wiki/Phenotypic_switching" title="Phenotypic switching">phenotypic switching</a> and grow as single cells in some environments, and <a href="/wiki/Hypha" title="Hypha">filamentous hyphae</a> in others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[65]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Plants">Plants</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microorganism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Plants">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Plant" title="Plant">Plant</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Green_algae" title="Green algae">green algae</a> are a large group of photosynthetic eukaryotes that include many microscopic organisms. Although some green algae are classified as <a href="/wiki/Protist" title="Protist">protists</a>, others such as <a href="/wiki/Charophyta" title="Charophyta">charophyta</a> are classified with <a href="/wiki/Embryophyte" title="Embryophyte">embryophyte</a> plants, which are the most familiar group of land plants. Algae can grow as single cells, or in long chains of cells. The green algae include unicellular and colonial <a href="/wiki/Flagellate" title="Flagellate">flagellates</a>, usually but not always with two <a href="/wiki/Flagellum" title="Flagellum">flagella</a> per cell, as well as various colonial, <a href="/wiki/Chlorococcales" title="Chlorococcales">coccoid</a>, and filamentous forms. In the <a href="/wiki/Charales" title="Charales">Charales</a>, which are the algae most closely related to higher plants, cells differentiate into several distinct tissues within the organism. There are about 6000 species of green algae.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[66]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ecology">Ecology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microorganism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Ecology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Microbial_ecology" title="Microbial ecology">Microbial ecology</a></div>
<p>Microorganisms are found in almost every <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Habitat_(ecology)" title="Habitat (ecology)">habitat</a> present in nature, including hostile environments such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Geographic_poles" title="Geographic poles">North and South poles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Desert" title="Desert">deserts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Geyser" title="Geyser">geysers</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rock_(geology)" title="Rock (geology)">rocks</a>. They also include all the <a href="/wiki/Marine_microorganism" title="Marine microorganism">marine microorganisms</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_ocean" title="World ocean">oceans</a> and <a href="/wiki/Deep_sea" title="Deep sea">deep sea</a>. Some types of microorganisms have adapted to <a href="/wiki/Extreme_environment" title="Extreme environment">extreme environments</a> and sustained colonies; these organisms are known as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extremophiles" title="Extremophiles">extremophiles</a>. Extremophiles have been isolated from rocks as much as 7 kilometres below the Earth's surface,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[67]</a></sup> and it has been suggested that the amount of organisms living below the Earth's surface is comparable with the amount of life on or above the surface.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gold_49-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gold-49">[48]</a></sup> Extremophiles have been known to survive for a prolonged time in a <a href="/wiki/Vacuum" title="Vacuum">vacuum</a>, and can be highly resistant to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ultraviolet_radiation" title="Ultraviolet radiation">radiation</a>, which may even allow them to survive in space.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[68]</a></sup> Many types of microorganisms have intimate <a href="/wiki/Symbiosis" title="Symbiosis">symbiotic relationships</a> with other larger organisms; some of which are mutually beneficial (<a href="/wiki/Mutualism_(biology)" title="Mutualism (biology)">mutualism</a>), while others can be damaging to the <a href="/wiki/Host_(biology)" title="Host (biology)">host</a> organism (<a href="/wiki/Parasitism" title="Parasitism">parasitism</a>). If microorganisms can cause <a href="/wiki/Disease" title="Disease">disease</a> in a host they are known as <a href="/wiki/Pathogen" title="Pathogen">pathogens</a> and then they are sometimes referred to as <i>microbes</i>.
Microorganisms play critical roles in Earth's <a href="/wiki/Biogeochemical_cycle" title="Biogeochemical cycle">biogeochemical cycles</a> as they are responsible for <a href="/wiki/Decomposition" title="Decomposition">decomposition</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nitrogen_fixation" title="Nitrogen fixation">nitrogen fixation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[69]</a></sup>
</p><p>Bacteria use <a href="/wiki/Gene_regulatory_network" title="Gene regulatory network">regulatory networks</a> that allow them to adapt to almost every environmental niche on earth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FillouxAAM_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-FillouxAAM-71">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GrossRBeierD_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-GrossRBeierD-72">[71]</a></sup> A network of interactions among diverse types of molecules including DNA, RNA, proteins and metabolites, is utilised by the bacteria to achieve <a href="/wiki/Regulation_of_gene_expression" title="Regulation of gene expression">regulation of gene expression</a>. In bacteria, the principal function of regulatory networks is to control the response to environmental changes, for example nutritional status and environmental stress.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RequenaJM_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-RequenaJM-73">[72]</a></sup> A complex organization of networks permits the microorganism to coordinate and integrate multiple environmental signals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FillouxAAM_71-1"><a href="#cite_note-FillouxAAM-71">[70]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Extremophiles">Extremophiles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microorganism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Extremophiles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Extremophile" title="Extremophile">Extremophile</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_microorganisms_tested_in_outer_space" title="List of microorganisms tested in outer space">List of microorganisms tested in outer space</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Deinococcus_radiodurans.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="612" data-file-width="532" height="196" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Deinococcus_radiodurans.jpg/170px-Deinococcus_radiodurans.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Deinococcus_radiodurans.jpg/255px-Deinococcus_radiodurans.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Deinococcus_radiodurans.jpg/340px-Deinococcus_radiodurans.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Deinococcus_radiodurans.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A tetrad of <i><a href="/wiki/Deinococcus_radiodurans" title="Deinococcus radiodurans">Deinococcus radiodurans</a></i>, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Radioresistant" title="Radioresistant">radioresistant</a> <a href="/wiki/Extremophile" title="Extremophile">extremophile</a> bacterium</div></div></div>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extremophiles" title="Extremophiles">Extremophiles</a> are microorganisms that have adapted so that they can survive and even thrive in <a href="/wiki/Extreme_environment" title="Extreme environment">extreme environments</a> that are normally fatal to most life-forms. <a href="/wiki/Thermophile" title="Thermophile">Thermophiles</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hyperthermophiles" title="Hyperthermophiles">hyperthermophiles</a> thrive in high <a href="/wiki/Temperature" title="Temperature">temperatures</a>. <a href="/wiki/Psychrophile" title="Psychrophile">Psychrophiles</a> thrive in extremely low temperatures. – Temperatures as high as 130 °C (266 °F),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[73]</a></sup> as low as −17 °C (1 °F)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[74]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Halophile" title="Halophile">Halophiles</a> such as <i><a href="/wiki/Halobacterium_salinarum" title="Halobacterium salinarum">Halobacterium salinarum</a></i> (an archaean) thrive in high <a href="/wiki/Salinity" title="Salinity">salt conditions</a>, up to saturation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[75]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Alkaliphile" title="Alkaliphile">Alkaliphiles</a> thrive in an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alkaline" title="Alkaline">alkaline</a> <a href="/wiki/PH" title="PH">pH</a> of about 8.5–11.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[76]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Acidophile" title="Acidophile">Acidophiles</a> can thrive in a pH of 2.0 or less.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[77]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Piezophile" title="Piezophile">Piezophiles</a> thrive at very <a href="/wiki/High_pressure" title="High pressure">high pressures</a>: up to 1,000–2,000 <a href="/wiki/Atmosphere_(unit)" title="Atmosphere (unit)">atm</a>, down to 0 atm as in a <a href="/wiki/Vacuum" title="Vacuum">vacuum</a> of <a href="/wiki/Outer_space" title="Outer space">space</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[78]</a></sup> A few extremophiles such as <i><a href="/wiki/Deinococcus_radiodurans" title="Deinococcus radiodurans">Deinococcus radiodurans</a></i> are <a href="/wiki/Radioresistance" title="Radioresistance">radioresistant</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[79]</a></sup> resisting <a href="/wiki/Ionizing_radiation" title="Ionizing radiation">radiation</a> exposure of up to 5k <a href="/wiki/Gray_(unit)" title="Gray (unit)">Gy</a>. Extremophiles are significant in different ways. They extend terrestrial life into much of the Earth's <a href="/wiki/Hydrosphere" title="Hydrosphere">hydrosphere</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crust_(geology)" title="Crust (geology)">crust</a> and <a href="/wiki/Atmosphere" title="Atmosphere">atmosphere</a>, their specific evolutionary adaptation mechanisms to their extreme environment can be exploited in <a href="/wiki/Biotechnology" title="Biotechnology">biotechnology</a>, and their very existence under such extreme conditions increases the potential for <a href="/wiki/Extraterrestrial_life" title="Extraterrestrial life">extraterrestrial life</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[80]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="In_soil">In soil</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microorganism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: In soil">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Soil_biology" title="Soil biology">Soil biology</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Nitrogen_cycle" title="Nitrogen cycle">nitrogen cycle</a> in soils depends on the <a href="/wiki/Nitrogen_fixation" title="Nitrogen fixation">fixation of atmospheric nitrogen</a>. This is achieved by a number of <a href="/wiki/Diazotroph" title="Diazotroph">diazotrophs</a>. One way this can occur is in the nodules in the roots of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Legumes" title="Legumes">legumes</a> that contain symbiotic <a href="/wiki/Bacteria" title="Bacteria">bacteria</a> of the genera <i><a href="/wiki/Rhizobium" title="Rhizobium">Rhizobium</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Mesorhizobium" title="Mesorhizobium">Mesorhizobium</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Sinorhizobium" title="Sinorhizobium">Sinorhizobium</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Bradyrhizobium" title="Bradyrhizobium">Bradyrhizobium</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Azorhizobium" title="Azorhizobium">Azorhizobium</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[81]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Symbiosis">Symbiosis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microorganism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Symbiosis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hyella_caespitosa.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1680" data-file-width="2240" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Hyella_caespitosa.jpg/220px-Hyella_caespitosa.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Hyella_caespitosa.jpg/330px-Hyella_caespitosa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Hyella_caespitosa.jpg/440px-Hyella_caespitosa.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hyella_caespitosa.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The photosynthetic <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cyanobacterium" title="Cyanobacterium">cyanobacterium</a> <i>Hyella caespitosa</i> (round shapes) with fungal hyphae (translucent threads) in the <a href="/wiki/Lichen" title="Lichen">lichen</a> <i>Pyrenocollema halodytes</i></div></div></div>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Lichen" title="Lichen">lichen</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Symbiosis" title="Symbiosis">symbiosis</a> of a macroscopic fungus with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Photosynthetic" title="Photosynthetic">photosynthetic</a> microbial <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alga" title="Alga">algae</a> or <a href="/wiki/Cyanobacteria" title="Cyanobacteria">cyanobacteria</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[82]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[83]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Applications">Applications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microorganism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Applications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Human_interactions_with_microbes" title="Human interactions with microbes">Human interactions with microbes</a></div>
<p>Microorganisms are useful in producing foods, treating waste water, creating biofuels and a wide range of chemicals and enzymes. They are invaluable in research as <a href="/wiki/Model_organism" title="Model organism">model organisms</a>. They have been <a href="/wiki/Biological_agent" title="Biological agent">weaponised</a> and sometimes used in <a href="/wiki/Biological_warfare" title="Biological warfare">warfare</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bioterrorism" title="Bioterrorism">bioterrorism</a>. They are vital to agriculture through their roles in maintaining soil fertility and in decomposing organic matter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[84]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Food_production">Food production</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microorganism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Food production">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Fermentation_in_food_processing" title="Fermentation in food processing">Fermentation in food processing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Food_microbiology" title="Food microbiology">Food microbiology</a></div>
<p>Microorganisms are used in a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fermentation_(food)" title="Fermentation (food)">fermentation</a> process to make <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yoghurt" title="Yoghurt">yoghurt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cheese" title="Cheese">cheese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Curd" title="Curd">curd</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kefir" title="Kefir">kefir</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ayran" title="Ayran">ayran</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fermented_milk_products" title="Fermented milk products">xynogala</a>, and other types of food. Fermentation cultures provide flavor and aroma, and inhibit undesirable organisms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[85]</a></sup> They are used to <a href="/wiki/Leavening_agent" title="Leavening agent">leaven</a> <a href="/wiki/Bread" title="Bread">bread</a>, and to convert <a href="/wiki/Sugar" title="Sugar">sugars</a> to <a href="/wiki/Alcohol" title="Alcohol">alcohol</a> in <a href="/wiki/Wine" title="Wine">wine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Beer" title="Beer">beer</a>. Microorganisms are used in <a href="/wiki/Brewing" title="Brewing">brewing</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wine_making" title="Wine making">wine making</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baking" title="Baking">baking</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pickling" title="Pickling">pickling</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Food" title="Food">food</a>-making processes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HuiMeunier-Goddik2004_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-HuiMeunier-Goddik2004-87">[86]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Water_treatment">Water treatment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microorganism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Water treatment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wastewater_treatment" title="Wastewater treatment">Wastewater treatment</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Drinking_water#Water_quality" title="Drinking water">Drinking water § Water quality</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:WWTP_Antwerpen-Zuid.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2085" data-file-width="2810" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/WWTP_Antwerpen-Zuid.jpg/220px-WWTP_Antwerpen-Zuid.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/WWTP_Antwerpen-Zuid.jpg/330px-WWTP_Antwerpen-Zuid.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/WWTP_Antwerpen-Zuid.jpg/440px-WWTP_Antwerpen-Zuid.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:WWTP_Antwerpen-Zuid.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Wastewater_treatment" title="Wastewater treatment">Wastewater treatment plants</a> rely largely on microorganisms to oxidise organic matter.</div></div></div>
<p>Sewage treatment works depend for their ability to clean up water contaminated with organic material on microorganisms that can respire dissolved substances. Respiration may be aerobic, with a well-oxygenated filter bed such as a <a href="/wiki/Slow_sand_filter" title="Slow sand filter">slow sand filter</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[87]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Anaerobic_digestion" title="Anaerobic digestion">Anaerobic digestion</a> by <a href="/wiki/Methanogen" title="Methanogen">methanogens</a> generate useful <a href="/wiki/Methane" title="Methane">methane</a> gas as a by-product.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[88]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microorganism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Algae_fuel" title="Algae fuel">Algae fuel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cellulosic_ethanol" title="Cellulosic ethanol">Cellulosic ethanol</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ethanol_fermentation" title="Ethanol fermentation">Ethanol fermentation</a></div>
<p>Microorganisms are used in <a href="/wiki/Ethanol_fermentation" title="Ethanol fermentation">fermentation to produce ethanol</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[89]</a></sup> and in <a href="/wiki/Biogas" title="Biogas">biogas</a> reactors to produce <a href="/wiki/Methane" title="Methane">methane</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[90]</a></sup> Scientists are researching the use of <a href="/wiki/Algae_fuel" title="Algae fuel">algae to produce liquid fuels</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[91]</a></sup> and bacteria to convert various forms of agricultural and urban waste into <a href="/wiki/Cellulosic_ethanol" title="Cellulosic ethanol">usable fuels</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[92]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Chemicals.2C_enzymes"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Chemicals,_enzymes">Chemicals, enzymes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microorganism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Chemicals, enzymes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Synthesis_of_nanoparticles_by_fungi" title="Synthesis of nanoparticles by fungi">Synthesis of nanoparticles by fungi</a></div>
<p>Microorganisms are used to produce many commercial and industrial chemicals, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Enzymes" title="Enzymes">enzymes</a> and other bioactive molecules. Organic acids produced on a large industrial scale by microbial fermentation include <a href="/wiki/Acetic_acid" title="Acetic acid">acetic acid</a> produced by <a href="/wiki/Acetic_acid_bacteria" title="Acetic acid bacteria">acetic acid bacteria</a> such as <i><a href="/wiki/Acetobacter_aceti" title="Acetobacter aceti">Acetobacter aceti</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Butyric_acid" title="Butyric acid">butyric acid</a> made by the bacterium <i><a href="/wiki/Clostridium_butyricum" title="Clostridium butyricum">Clostridium butyricum</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Lactic_acid" title="Lactic acid">lactic acid</a> made by <i><a href="/wiki/Lactobacillus" title="Lactobacillus">Lactobacillus</a></i> and other <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lactic_acid_bacteria" title="Lactic acid bacteria">lactic acid bacteria</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sauer_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sauer-94">[93]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Citric_acid" title="Citric acid">citric acid</a> produced by the mould fungus <i><a href="/wiki/Aspergillus_niger" title="Aspergillus niger">Aspergillus niger</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sauer_94-1"><a href="#cite_note-Sauer-94">[93]</a></sup>
</p><p>Microorganisms are used to prepare bioactive molecules such as <a href="/wiki/Streptokinase" title="Streptokinase">Streptokinase</a> from the bacterium <i><a href="/wiki/Streptococcus" title="Streptococcus">Streptococcus</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[94]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cyclosporin_A" title="Cyclosporin A">Cyclosporin A</a> from the ascomycete fungus <i><a href="/wiki/Tolypocladium_inflatum" title="Tolypocladium inflatum">Tolypocladium inflatum</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[95]</a></sup> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Statins" title="Statins">statins</a> produced by the yeast <i><a href="/wiki/Monascus_purpureus" title="Monascus purpureus">Monascus purpureus</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[96]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Science">Science</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microorganism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Science">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Biofermentor.jpeg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Biofermentor.jpeg/220px-Biofermentor.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Biofermentor.jpeg/330px-Biofermentor.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Biofermentor.jpeg/440px-Biofermentor.jpeg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Biofermentor.jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A laboratory <a href="/wiki/Fermentation" title="Fermentation">fermentation</a> vessel</div></div></div>
<p>Microorganisms are essential tools in <a href="/wiki/Biotechnology" title="Biotechnology">biotechnology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Biochemistry" title="Biochemistry">biochemistry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Genetics" title="Genetics">genetics</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Molecular_biology" title="Molecular biology">molecular biology</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Yeast" title="Yeast">yeasts</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Saccharomyces_cerevisiae" title="Saccharomyces cerevisiae">Saccharomyces cerevisiae</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Schizosaccharomyces_pombe" title="Schizosaccharomyces pombe">Schizosaccharomyces pombe</a></i> are important <a href="/wiki/Model_organism" title="Model organism">model organisms</a> in science, since they are simple eukaryotes that can be grown rapidly in large numbers and are easily manipulated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[97]</a></sup> They are particularly valuable in <a href="/wiki/Genetics" title="Genetics">genetics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Genomics" title="Genomics">genomics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Proteomics" title="Proteomics">proteomics</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[98]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[99]</a></sup> Microorganisms can be harnessed for uses such as creating steroids and treating skin diseases. Scientists are also considering using microorganisms for living <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fuel_cells" title="Fuel cells">fuel cells</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[100]</a></sup> and as a solution for pollution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[101]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Warfare">Warfare</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microorganism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Warfare">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Biological_warfare" title="Biological warfare">Biological warfare</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bioterrorism" title="Bioterrorism">Bioterrorism</a></div>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>, as an early example of <a href="/wiki/Biological_warfare" title="Biological warfare">biological warfare</a>, diseased corpses were thrown into castles during <a href="/wiki/Siege" title="Siege">sieges</a> using catapults or other <a href="/wiki/Siege_engine" title="Siege engine">siege engines</a>. Individuals near the corpses were exposed to the pathogen and were likely to spread that pathogen to others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[102]</a></sup>
</p><p>In modern times, <a href="/wiki/Bioterrorism" title="Bioterrorism">bioterrorism</a> has included the <a href="/wiki/1984_Rajneeshee_bioterror_attack" title="1984 Rajneeshee bioterror attack">1984 Rajneeshee bioterror attack</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[103]</a></sup> and the 1993 release of <a href="/wiki/Anthrax" title="Anthrax">anthrax</a> by <a href="/wiki/Aum_Shinrikyo" title="Aum Shinrikyo">Aum Shinrikyo</a> in Tokyo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[104]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Soil">Soil</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microorganism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Soil">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Soil_microbiology" title="Soil microbiology">Soil microbiology</a></div><p>Microbes can make <a href="/wiki/Nutrient" title="Nutrient">nutrients</a> and minerals in the soil available to plants, produce <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hormones" title="Hormones">hormones</a> that spur growth, stimulate the plant <a href="/wiki/Immune_system" title="Immune system">immune system</a> and trigger or dampen stress responses. In general a more diverse set of <a href="/wiki/Soil_biology" title="Soil biology">soil</a> microbes results in fewer plant diseases and higher yield.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:02_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-:02-106">[105]</a></sup>
</p><h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_health">Human health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microorganism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Human health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_gut_flora">Human gut flora</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microorganism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Human gut flora">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Human_microbiota" title="Human microbiota">Human microbiota</a> and <a href="/wiki/Human_Microbiome_Project" title="Human Microbiome Project">Human Microbiome Project</a></div>
<p>Microorganisms can form an <a href="/wiki/Endosymbiont" title="Endosymbiont">endosymbiotic</a> relationship with other, larger organisms. For example, <a href="/wiki/Microbial_symbiosis_and_immunity" title="Microbial symbiosis and immunity">microbial symbiosis</a> plays a crucial role in the immune system. The microorganisms that make up the <a href="/wiki/Gut_flora" title="Gut flora">gut flora</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Gastrointestinal_tract" title="Gastrointestinal tract">gastrointestinal tract</a> contribute to gut immunity, synthesize <a href="/wiki/Vitamin" title="Vitamin">vitamins</a> such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Folic_acid" title="Folic acid">folic acid</a> and <a href="/wiki/Biotin" title="Biotin">biotin</a>, and ferment complex indigestible <a href="/wiki/Carbohydrate" title="Carbohydrate">carbohydrates</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[106]</a></sup> Some microorganisms that are seen to be beneficial to health are termed <a href="/wiki/Probiotic" title="Probiotic">probiotics</a> and are available as <a href="/wiki/Dietary_supplement" title="Dietary supplement">dietary supplements</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Food_additive#Fortifying_agents" title="Food additive">food additives</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-who_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-who-108">[107]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Disease">Disease</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microorganism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Disease">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Pathogen" title="Pathogen">Pathogen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Germ_theory_of_disease" title="Germ theory of disease">Germ theory of disease</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Medical_microbiology" title="Medical microbiology">Medical microbiology</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parasite" title="Parasite">Parasite</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Plasmodium.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="473" data-file-width="440" height="183" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Plasmodium.jpg/170px-Plasmodium.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Plasmodium.jpg/255px-Plasmodium.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Plasmodium.jpg/340px-Plasmodium.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Plasmodium.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eukaryotic" title="Eukaryotic">eukaryotic</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parasite" title="Parasite">parasite</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Plasmodium_falciparum" title="Plasmodium falciparum">Plasmodium falciparum</a></i> (spiky blue shapes), a causative agent of <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">malaria</a>, in human <a href="/wiki/Blood" title="Blood">blood</a></div></div></div>
<p>Microorganisms are the causative agents (<a href="/wiki/Pathogen" title="Pathogen">pathogens</a>) in many <a href="/wiki/Infection" title="Infection">infectious diseases</a>. The organisms involved include <a href="/wiki/Pathogenic_bacteria" title="Pathogenic bacteria">pathogenic bacteria</a>, causing diseases such as <a href="/wiki/Bubonic_plague" title="Bubonic plague">plague</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tuberculosis" title="Tuberculosis">tuberculosis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anthrax" title="Anthrax">anthrax</a>; <a href="/wiki/Protozoa" title="Protozoa">protozoan</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parasite" title="Parasite">parasites</a>, causing diseases such as <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">malaria</a>, <a href="/wiki/African_trypanosomiasis" title="African trypanosomiasis">sleeping sickness</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dysentery" title="Dysentery">dysentery</a> and <a href="/wiki/Toxoplasmosis" title="Toxoplasmosis">toxoplasmosis</a>; and also fungi causing diseases such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ringworm" title="Ringworm">ringworm</a>, <a href="/wiki/Candidiasis" title="Candidiasis">candidiasis</a> or <a href="/wiki/Histoplasmosis" title="Histoplasmosis">histoplasmosis</a>. However, other diseases such as <a href="/wiki/Influenza" title="Influenza">influenza</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yellow_fever" title="Yellow fever">yellow fever</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AIDS" title="AIDS">AIDS</a> are caused by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pathogenic_viruses" title="Pathogenic viruses">pathogenic viruses</a>, which are not usually classified as living organisms and are not, therefore, microorganisms by the strict definition. No clear examples of archaean pathogens are known,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[108]</a></sup> although a relationship has been proposed between the presence of some archaean methanogens and human <a href="/wiki/Periodontal_disease" title="Periodontal disease">periodontal disease</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[109]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hygiene">Hygiene</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microorganism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Hygiene">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Hygiene" title="Hygiene">Hygiene</a> and <a href="/wiki/Food_microbiology" title="Food microbiology">Food microbiology</a></div>
<p>Hygiene is a set of practices to avoid <a href="/wiki/Infection" title="Infection">infection</a> or <a href="/wiki/Food_spoilage" title="Food spoilage">food spoilage</a> by eliminating microorganisms from the surroundings. As microorganisms, in particular <a href="/wiki/Bacteria" title="Bacteria">bacteria</a>, are found virtually everywhere, <a href="/wiki/Pathogen" title="Pathogen">harmful microorganisms</a> may be reduced to acceptable levels rather than actually eliminated. In food preparation, microorganisms are reduced by <a href="/wiki/Food_preservation" title="Food preservation">preservation</a> methods such as cooking, cleanliness of utensils, short storage periods, or by low temperatures. If complete sterility is needed, as with surgical equipment, an <a href="/wiki/Autoclave" title="Autoclave">autoclave</a> is used to kill microorganisms with heat and pressure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[110]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[111]</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microorganism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The word <i>microorganism</i> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˌ/: secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/aɪ/: 'i' in 'tide'">aɪ</span><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="'r' in 'rye'">r</span><span title="/oʊ/: 'o' in 'code'">oʊ</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/ɔːr/: 'ar' in 'war'">ɔːr</span><span title="/ɡ/: 'g' in 'guy'">ɡ</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">ɪ</span><span title="'z' in 'zoom'">z</span><span title="/əm/: 'm' in 'rhythm'">əm</span></span>/</a></span></span>) uses <a href="/wiki/Classical_compound" title="Classical compound">combining forms</a> of <i><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/micro-#Prefix" title="wikt:micro-">micro-</a></i> (from the <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a>: <span lang="el">μικρός</span>, <i>mikros</i>, "small") and <i><a href="/wiki/Organism" title="Organism">organism</a></i> from the <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a>: <span lang="el">ὀργανισμός</span>, <i>organismós</i>, "organism"). It is usually styled solid but is sometimes <a href="/wiki/Hyphen" title="Hyphen">hyphenated</a> (<i>micro-organism</i>), especially in older texts. The informal synonym <i>microbe</i> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/aɪ/: 'i' in 'tide'">aɪ</span><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="'r' in 'rye'">r</span><span title="/oʊ/: 'o' in 'code'">oʊ</span><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span></span>/</a></span></span>) comes from  μικρός, mikrós, "small" and βίος, bíos, "<a href="/wiki/Life" title="Life">life</a>".</span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microorganism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<ul><li><a class="external text" href="http://www.microbes.info/" rel="nofollow">Microbes.info</a> is a microbiology information portal containing a vast collection of resources including articles, news, frequently asked questions, and links pertaining to the field of microbiology.</li>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://dels.nas.edu/metagenomics" rel="nofollow">Our Microbial Planet</a> A free poster from the National Academy of Sciences about the positive roles of micro-organisms.</li>
<li><a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20080527234727/http://www.asm.org/ASM/files/ccLibraryFiles/Filename/000000003691/Uncharted_Microbial_World.pdf" rel="nofollow">"Uncharted Microbial World: Microbes and Their Activities in the Environment"</a> Report from the American Academy of Microbiology</li>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://dels.nas.edu/dels/rpt_briefs/metagenomics_final.pdf" rel="nofollow">Understanding Our Microbial Planet: The New Science of Metagenomics</a> A 20-page educational booklet providing a basic overview of metagenomics and our microbial planet.</li>
